26 SECTION 1.(c) G.S. 50-11 reads as rewritten:
27 "§ 50-11. Effects of absolute divorce.
28 (a) After a judgment of divorce from the bonds of matrimony, all rights arising out of the
29 marriage shall cease and determine except as hereinafter set out, cease, except as otherwise
30 provided by this section, and either party may marry again without restriction arising from the
31 dissolved marriage.
32 (b) No judgment of divorce shall cause any child in esse or begotten of the body of the
33 wife during coverture the marriage to be treated as a child born out of wedlock.
34 (c) A divorce obtained pursuant to G.S. 50-5.1 or G.S. 50-6 shall does not affect the
35 rights of either spouse with respect to any action for alimony or postseparation support pending
36 at the time the judgment for divorce is granted. Furthermore, a judgment of absolute divorce shall
37 does not impair or destroy the right of a spouse to receive alimony or postseparation support or
38 affect any other rights provided for such the spouse under any judgment or decree of a court
39 rendered before or at the time of the judgment of absolute divorce.
40 (d) A divorce obtained outside the State in an action in which jurisdiction over the person
41 of the dependent spouse was not obtained shall does not impair or destroy the right of the
42 dependent spouse to alimony as provided by the laws of this State.
43 (e) An absolute divorce obtained within in this State shall destroy destroys the right of a
44 spouse to equitable distribution under G.S. 50-20 unless the right is asserted prior to judgment of
45 absolute divorce; except, however, the defendant may bring an action or file a motion in the cause
46 for equitable distribution within six months from the date of the judgment in such a the case if
47 service of process upon the defendant was by publication pursuant to G.S. 1A-1, Rule 4 Rule 4,
48 and the defendant failed to appear in the action for divorce.
49 (f) An absolute divorce by a court that lacked personal jurisdiction over the absent spouse
50 or lacked jurisdiction to dispose of the property shall does not destroy the right of a spouse to
51 equitable distribution under G.S. 50-20 if an action or motion in the cause is filed within six

4 "§ 52-10. Contracts between husband and wife generally; releases.
5 (a) Contracts between husband and wife not inconsistent with public policy are valid, and
6 any persons of full age about to be married and married persons may, with or without a valuable
7 consideration, release and quitclaim such rights which they might respectively acquire or may
8 have acquired by marriage in the property of each other; and such other. These releases may be
9 pleaded in bar of any action or proceeding for the recovery of the rights and estate so released.

11 affect or change any part of the real estate of either spouse, or the accruing income thereof for a
12 longer time than three years next ensuing the making of such contract or release, marriage affects

14 certifying officer.officer:
15 (1) Either spouse's real property.
16 (2) Income from either spouse's real property accruing more than three years after
17 the execution of the contract or release.

19 consideration, during a period of separation to waive, release, or establish rights and obligations
20 to post separation postseparation support, alimony, or spousal support is valid and not
21 inconsistent with public policy. A provision waiving, releasing, or establishing rights and
22 obligations to post separation postseparation support, alimony, or spousal support shall remain
23 remains valid following a period of reconciliation and subsequent separation, if the contract
24 satisfies all of the following requirements:
25 (1) The contract is in writing.
26 (2) The provision waiving the rights or obligations is clearly stated in the contract.
27 (3) The contract was acknowledged by both parties before a certifying officer.
28 A release made pursuant to this subsection may be pleaded in bar of any action or proceeding for
29 the recovery of the rights released.

34 "§ 143-215.94V. Standards for petroleum underground storage tank cleanup.
35 (a) Legislative findings and intent.

12 (a) Basic Rate. – The maximum monthly rate for State-County Special Assistance

14 Alzheimer's disease or dementia shall be one thousand one hundred eighty-two dollars ($1,182)
15 is one thousand two hundred eighty-five dollars ($1,285) per month per resident. This rate shall

17 Security cost-of-living adjustment effective for the applicable year.

20 Alzheimer's disease or dementia shall be one thousand five hundred fifteen dollars ($1,515) is
21 one thousand six hundred forty-seven dollars ($1,647) per month per resident. This rate shall be
22 adjusted on January 1, 2024, and each January 1 thereafter, using the federally approved Social
23 Security cost-of-living adjustment effective for the applicable year."

25 SECTION 28.(a) Section 9A.3A(a) of S.L. 2021-180 reads as rewritten:
26 "SECTION 9A.3A.(a) It is the intent of the General Assembly to provide greater parity
27 among individuals receiving benefits under the State-County Special Assistance Program
28 authorized under G.S. 108A-40 regardless if they elect to reside in an adult care home, a special
29 care unit, or an in-home living arrangement. To that end, no later than 30 days after the effective
30 date of this subsection, the Department of Health and Human Services, Division of Aging and
31 Adult Services, shall apply to the federal Social Security Administration (SSA) for approval to
32 allow eligible individuals residing in in-home living arrangements to qualify for State-County
33 Special Assistance under the Social Security Optional State Supplement Program in the same
34 manner as individuals residing in adult care homes or special care units. Additionally, no later
35 than 30 days after the effective date of this subsection, the Department of Health and Human
36 Services, Division of Health Benefits, shall submit a State Plan amendment to the Centers for
37 Medicare and Medicaid Services (CMS) for approval to add Medicaid coverage for individuals
38 residing in in-home living arrangements who qualify for State-County Special Assistance under
39 the Social Security Optional State Supplement Program. It is the further intent of the General
40 Assembly to appropriate sufficient funds in future fiscal years to support annual adjustment of
41 the State-County Special Assistance Program payment rates using the federally approved Social
42 Security cost-of-living adjustment. This subsection is effective when it becomes law."

27 certified mail, or email" in G.S. 143-293.

29 in G.S. 14-113.20, 14-113.30, 14-113.31, 14-118.7, 14-196.3, and any other

36 in which any of these terms appear. The Revisor of Statutes shall make a
37 similar change when any of these terms is plural.
38 (6) Replace "rule making" or "rule-making" with "rulemaking" in G.S. 7B-4001,
39 10B-126, 15C-12, 18B-105, 20-37.22, and any other statutes in which either
40 of these terms appear.

42 and may replace "an" with "a" to conform with these changes.

16 SECTION 34.(a) Part 1 of Article 45 of Chapter 66 of the General Statutes reads as
17 rewritten:
18 "Part 1. Pawnbrokers and Cash Currency Converters.
19 "§ 66-385. Short title.
20 This Part shall be known and may be cited as the Pawnbrokers and Cash Currency Converters
21 Modernization Act.
22 "§ 66-386. Purpose.
23 The making of pawn loans and the acquisition and disposition of tangible personal property
24 by and through pawnshops and cash currency converters vitally affects the general economy of
25 this State and the public interest and welfare of its citizens. In recognition of these facts, it is the
26 policy of this State and the purpose of the Pawnbrokers and Cash Converters Modernization Act
27 this Part to do all of the following:
28 (1) Ensure a sound system of making loans and acquiring and disposing of
29 tangible personal property by and through pawnshops, pawnshops and to
30 prevent unlawful property transactions, particularly in stolen property,
31 through licensing and regulating pawnbrokers.
32 (2) Ensure a sound system of acquiring and disposing of tangible personal
33 property by and through cash currency converters and to prevent unlawful
34 property transactions, particularly in stolen property, by requiring record
35 keeping by cash currency converters.
36 (3) Provide for pawnbroker licensing fees and investigation fees of licensees.
37 (4) Ensure financial responsibility to the State and the general public.
38 (5) Ensure compliance with federal and State laws.
39 (6) Assist local governments in the exercise of their police authority.

4 SECTION 35.(c) G.S. 75D-5 reads as rewritten:
5 "§ 75D-5. RICO civil forfeiture proceedings.
6 (a) All property of every kind used or intended for use in the course of, derived from, or
7 realized through a racketeering activity or pattern of racketeering activity is subject to forfeiture
8 to the State. Forfeiture shall be had by a civil procedure known as a RICO forfeiture proceeding.
9 (b) A RICO forfeiture proceeding shall be is governed by Chapter 1A of the General
10 Statutes of North Carolina except to the extent that special rules of procedure are stated in this
11 Chapter.
12 (c) A RICO forfeiture proceeding shall be is an in rem proceeding against the property.
13 (d) A RICO forfeiture proceeding shall be instituted by complaint and prosecuted only
14 by the Attorney General of North Carolina or his designated representative. General. The
15 proceeding may be commenced and a final judgment rendered thereon before or after seizure of
16 the property and before or after any a criminal conviction of any person for violation of those
17 laws any law set forth in G.S. 75D-3(c).G.S. 75D-3(8).
18 (e) If the complaint is filed before seizure, it shall state what property is sought to be
19 forfeited, that the property is within the jurisdiction of the court, the grounds for forfeiture, and
20 the names of all persons known to have or claim an interest in the property. The court shall
21 determine ex parte whether there is reasonable ground to believe that the property is subject to
22 forfeiture and, if the State so alleges, whether notice to those persons having or claiming an
23 interest in the property prior to seizure would cause the loss or destruction of the property. If the
24 court finds:The court shall take action as follows:
25 (1) That If the court finds that reasonable ground does not exist to believe that the
26 property is subject to forfeiture, it shall dismiss the complaint; orcomplaint.
27 (2) That If the court finds that reasonable ground does exist to believe the property
28 is subject to forfeiture but there is not reasonable ground to believe that prior
29 notice would result in loss or destruction, it shall order service on all persons
30 known to have or claim an interest in the property prior to a further hearing
31 on whether a writ of seizure should issue; orissue.
32 (3) That If the court finds that there is reasonable ground to believe that the
33 property is subject to forfeiture and to believe that prior notice would cause
34 loss or destruction, it shall shall, without any further hearing or notice, issue a
35 writ of seizure directing the sheriff of or any other law enforcement officer in
36 the county where the property is found to seize it.
37 (f) Seizure may be effected by a law enforcement officer authorized to enforce the penal
38 laws of this State prior to the filing of the complaint and without a writ of seizure if the seizure
39 is incident to a lawful arrest, search, or inspection and the officer has probable cause to believe
40 the property is subject to forfeiture and will be lost or destroyed if not seized. Within 24 hours of
41 the time of seizure, the seizure shall be reported by the officer to the district attorney of the
42 prosecutorial district as defined in G.S. 7A-60 in which the seizure is effected who shall
43 immediately report such the seizure to the Attorney General. The Attorney General shall, within
44 30 days after receiving notice of seizure, examine the evidence surrounding such the seizure, and
45 if he the Attorney General believes reasonable ground exists for forfeiture under this Chapter,
46 the Attorney General shall file a complaint for forfeiture. The complaint shall state, in addition
47 to the information required in subsection (e) of this section, the date and place of seizure.
48 (g) After the complaint is filed or the seizure effected, whichever is later, every person
49 known to have or claim an interest in the property, or in the property or enterprise of which the
50 subject property is a part or represents any interest, shall be served, if not previously served, with

19 (1b) Ambulatory surgical facility. – A facility designed for the provision of a
20 specialty ambulatory surgical program or a multispecialty ambulatory surgical
21 program. An ambulatory surgical facility serves patients who require local,
22 regional, or general anesthesia and a period of post-operative observation. An
23 ambulatory surgical facility may only admit patients for a period of less than
24 24 hours and must shall provide at least one designated operating room or
25 gastrointestinal endoscopy room and at least one designated recovery room,
26 have available the necessary equipment and trained personnel to handle
27 emergencies, provide adequate quality assurance and assessment by an

25 SECTION 39.2.(b) Article 9 of Chapter 131E of the General Statutes is amended by
26 adding a new section to read:
27 "§ 131E-176.2. State Medical Facilities Plan.
28 The Department of Health and Human Services and the North Carolina State Health
29 Coordinating Council shall prepare and present to the Governor for approval the State Medical
30 Facilities Plan. In preparing the Plan, the Department and the State Health Coordinating Council
31 shall maintain a mailing list of persons that have requested notice of public hearings regarding
32 the Plan. Not less than 15 days prior to a scheduled public hearing, the Department shall notify
33 persons on its mailing list of the date, time, and location of the hearing. The Department shall
34 hold at least one public hearing prior to the adoption of the proposed Plan and at least six public
35 hearings after the adoption of the proposed Plan by the State Health Coordinating Council. The
36 Council shall accept oral and written comments from the public concerning the Plan."

6 "Uniform Child Abduction Prevention Act.
7 "§ 50A-411. Short title.
8 This Article may be cited as the Uniform Child Abduction Prevention Act.
9 "§ 50A-412. Definitions.
10 In this Article, the following definitions apply:
11 (1) Abduction. – The wrongful removal or wrongful retention of a child.
12 (2) Child. – Defined in G.S. 50A-102.
13 (3) Child-custody determination. – Defined in G.S. 50A-102.
14 (4) Child-custody proceeding. – Defined in G.S. 50A-102.
15 (5) Court. – Defined in G.S. 50A-102.
16 (6) Petition. – Includes a motion or its equivalent.
17 (7) Record. – Information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored
18 in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
19 (8) State. – Consists of the following:
20 a. A state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the
21 United States Virgin Islands, or any territory or insular possession
22 subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
23 b. An Indian tribe or band or Alaskan native village that is recognized by
24 federal law or formally acknowledged by an entity listed in
25 sub-subdivision a. of this subdivision.
26 (9) Travel documents. – Records relating to a travel itinerary, including travel
27 tickets, passes, reservations for transportation, or accommodations. The term
28 does not include a passport or visa.
29 (10) Wrongful removal. – The taking of a child that breaches rights of custody or
30 visitation given or recognized under the law of this State.
31 (11) Wrongful retention. – The keeping or concealing of a child that breaches rights
32 of custody or visitation given or recognized under the law of this State.
33 "§ 50A-413. Cooperation and communication among courts.
34 G.S. 50A-110, 50A-111, and 50A-112 apply to cooperation and communications among
35 courts in proceedings under this Article.
36 "§ 50A-414. Actions for abduction prevention measures.
37 (a) A court on its own motion may order abduction prevention measures in a
38 child-custody proceeding if the court finds that the evidence establishes a credible risk of
39 abduction of the child.
40 (b) A party to a child-custody determination or another individual or entity having a right
41 under the law of this State or any other state to seek a child-custody determination for the child
42 may file a petition seeking abduction prevention measures to protect the child under this Article.
43 "§ 50A-415. Jurisdiction.
44 (a) A petition under this Article may be filed in district court if the court has jurisdiction
45 to make a child-custody determination with respect to the child at issue under Article 2 of this
46 Chapter.
47 (b) A district court of this State has temporary emergency jurisdiction under
48 G.S. 50A-204 if the court finds a credible risk of abduction.
49 "§ 50A-416. Contents of petition.
50 A petition under this Article must be verified and include a copy of any existing child-custody
51 determination, if available. The petition must specify the risk factors for abduction, including the
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 89

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 relevant factors described in G.S. 50A-417. Subject to G.S. 50A-209(e), if reasonably
2 ascertainable, the petition must contain all of the following:
3 (1) The name, date of birth, and gender of the child.
4 (2) The customary address and current physical location of the child.
5 (3) The identity, customary address, and current physical location of the
6 respondent.
7 (4) A statement of whether a prior action to prevent abduction or domestic
8 violence has been filed by a party or other individual or entity having custody
9 of the child and the date, location, and disposition of the action.
10 (5) A statement of whether a party to the proceeding has been arrested for a crime
11 related to domestic violence, stalking, or child abuse or neglect and the date,
12 location, and disposition of the case.
13 (6) Any other information required to be submitted to the court for a child-custody
14 determination under G.S. 50-13.1(a1) or G.S. 50A-209.
15 "§ 50A-417. Factors to determine risk of abduction.
16 (a) In determining whether there is a credible risk of abduction of a child, the court must
17 consider any evidence that the petitioner or respondent has done or is doing any of the following:
18 (1) Has previously abducted or attempted to abduct the child.
19 (2) Has threatened to abduct the child.
20 (3) Has recently engaged in activities that may indicate a planned abduction,
21 including any of the following:
22 a. Abandoning employment.
23 b. Selling a primary residence.
24 c. Terminating a lease.
25 d. Closing bank or other financial management accounts, liquidating
26 assets, hiding or destroying financial documents, or conducting any
27 unusual financial activities.
28 e. Applying for a passport or visa or obtaining travel documents for the
29 respondent, a family member, or the child.
30 f. Seeking to obtain the child's birth certificate or school or medical
31 records.
32 (4) Has engaged in domestic violence, stalking, or child abuse or neglect.
33 (5) Has refused to follow a child-custody determination.
34 (6) Lacks strong familial, financial, emotional, or cultural ties to the State or the
35 United States.
36 (7) Has strong familial, financial, emotional, or cultural ties to another state or
37 country.
38 (8) Is likely to take the child to a country that meets any of the following
39 descriptions:
40 a. The country is not a party to the Hague Convention on the Civil
41 Aspects of International Child Abduction and does not provide for the
42 extradition of an abducting parent or for the return of an abducted
43 child.
44 b. The country is a party to the Hague Convention on the Civil Aspects
45 of International Child Abduction, but the country also meets any of the
46 following descriptions:
47 1. The Hague Convention on the Civil Aspects of International
48 Child Abduction is not in force between the United States and
49 the country.
Page 90 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 2. The country is noncompliant according to the most recent
2 compliance report issued by the United States Department of
3 State.
4 3. The country lacks legal mechanisms for immediately and
5 effectively enforcing a return order under the Hague
6 Convention on the Civil Aspects of International Child
7 Abduction.
8 c. The country poses a risk that the child's physical or emotional health
9 or safety would be endangered because of specific circumstances
10 relating to the child or because of human rights violations committed
11 against children.
12 d. The country has laws or practices that would do any of the following:
13 1. Enable the respondent, without due cause, to prevent the
14 petitioner from contacting the child.
15 2. Restrict the petitioner from freely traveling to or exiting from
16 the country because of the petitioner's gender, nationality,
17 marital status, or religion.
18 3. Restrict the child's ability legally to leave the country after the
19 child reaches the age of majority because of a child's gender,
20 nationality, or religion.
21 e. The country is included by the United States Department of State on a
22 current list of state sponsors of terrorism.
23 f. The country has no official United States diplomatic presence.
24 g. The country is engaged in active military action or war, including a
25 civil war, to which the child may be exposed.
26 (9) Is undergoing a change in immigration or citizenship status that would
27 adversely affect the person's ability to remain in the United States lawfully.
28 (10) Has had an application for United States citizenship denied.
29 (11) Has forged or presented misleading or false evidence on government forms or
30 supporting documents to obtain or attempt to obtain a passport, a visa, travel
31 documents, a social security card, a drivers license, or other
32 government-issued identification card or has made a misrepresentation to the
33 United States government.
34 (12) Has used multiple names to attempt to mislead or defraud.
35 (13) Has engaged in any other conduct the court considers relevant to the risk of
36 abduction.
37 (b) In the hearing on a petition under this Article, the court must consider any evidence
38 that the respondent believed in good faith that the respondent's conduct was necessary to avoid
39 imminent harm to the child or respondent and any other evidence that may be relevant to whether
40 the respondent may be permitted to remove or retain the child.
41 "§ 50A-418. Provisions and measures to prevent abduction.
42 (a) If a petition is filed under this Article, the court may enter an order that must include
43 all of the following:
44 (1) The basis for the court's exercise of jurisdiction.
45 (2) The manner in which notice and opportunity to be heard were given to the
46 persons entitled to notice of the proceeding.
47 (3) A detailed description of each party's custody and visitation rights and
48 residential arrangements for the child.
49 (4) A provision stating that a violation of the order may subject the party in
50 violation to civil and criminal penalties.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 91

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (5) Identification of the child's country of habitual residence at the time of the
2 issuance of the order.
3 (b) If, at a hearing on a petition under this Article or on the court's own motion, the court
4 after reviewing the evidence finds a credible risk of abduction of the child, the court must enter
5 an abduction prevention order. The order must include the provisions required by subsection (a)
6 of this section and measures and conditions, including those in subsections (c), (d), and (e) of
7 this section, that are reasonably calculated to prevent abduction of the child, giving due
8 consideration to the custody and visitation rights of the parties. The court must consider the age
9 of the child, the potential harm to the child from an abduction, the legal and practical difficulties
10 of returning the child to the jurisdiction if abducted, and the reasons for the potential abduction,
11 including evidence of domestic violence, stalking, or child abuse or neglect.
12 (c) An abduction prevention order may include one or more of the following:
13 (1) An imposition of travel restrictions that require that a party traveling with the
14 child outside a designated geographical area provide the other party with all
15 of the following:
16 a. The travel itinerary of the child.
17 b. A list of physical addresses and telephone numbers at which the child
18 can be reached at specified times.
19 c. Copies of all travel documents.
20 (2) A prohibition of the respondent directly or indirectly doing any of the
21 following:
22 a. Removing the child from this State, the United States, or another
23 geographic area without permission of the court or the petitioner's
24 written consent.
25 b. Removing or retaining the child in violation of a child-custody
26 determination.
27 c. Removing the child from school or a child-care or similar facility.
28 d. Approaching the child at any location other than a site designated for
29 supervised visitation.
30 (3) A requirement that a party register the order in another state as a prerequisite
31 to allowing the child to travel to that state.
32 (4) With regard to the child's passport, one or more of the following:
33 a. A direction that the petitioner place the child's name in the United
34 States Department of State's Child Passport Issuance Alert Program.
35 b. A requirement that the respondent surrender to the court or the
36 petitioner's attorney any United States or foreign passport issued in the
37 child's name, including a passport issued in the name of both the parent
38 and the child.
39 c. A prohibition upon the respondent from applying on behalf of the child
40 for a new or replacement passport or visa.
41 (5) As a prerequisite to exercising custody or visitation, a requirement that the
42 respondent provide all of the following:
43 a. To the United States Department of State Office of Children's Issues
44 and the relevant foreign consulate or embassy, an authenticated copy
45 of the order detailing passport and travel restrictions for the child.
46 b. To the court, both of the following:
47 1. Proof that the respondent has provided the information in
48 sub-subdivision a. of this subdivision.
49 2. An acknowledgment in a record from the relevant foreign
50 consulate or embassy that no passport application has been
51 made, or passport issued, on behalf of the child.
Page 92 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 c. To the petitioner, proof of registration of the order with the United
2 States Embassy or other United States diplomatic presence in the
3 destination country and with the Central Authority for the Hague
4 Convention on the Civil Aspects of International Child Abduction, if
5 that Convention is in effect between the United States and the
6 destination country, unless one of the parties objects.
7 d. A written waiver under the Privacy Act, 5 U.S.C. § 552a, with respect
8 to any document, application, or other information pertaining to the
9 child authorizing its disclosure to the court and the petitioner.
10 (6) Upon the petitioner's request, a requirement that the respondent obtain an
11 order from the relevant foreign country containing terms identical to the
12 child-custody determination issued in the United States.
13 (d) In an abduction prevention order, the court may impose conditions on the exercise of
14 custody or visitation that do one or more of the following:
15 (1) Limit visitation or require that visitation with the child by the respondent be
16 supervised until the court finds that supervision is no longer necessary and
17 order the respondent to pay the costs of supervision.
18 (2) Require the respondent to post a bond or provide other security in an amount
19 sufficient to serve as a financial deterrent to abduction, the proceeds of which
20 may be used to pay for the reasonable expenses of recovery of the child,
21 including reasonable attorneys' fees and costs if there is an abduction.
22 (3) Require the respondent to obtain education on the potentially harmful effects
23 to the child from abduction.
24 (e) To prevent imminent abduction of a child, a court may do any of the following:
25 (1) Issue a warrant to take physical custody of the child under G.S. 50A-419 or
26 other State law.
27 (2) Authorize law enforcement to take any action reasonably necessary to locate
28 the child or obtain return of the child pursuant to an order issued under this
29 Article or other State law.
30 (3) Grant any other relief allowed under other State law.
31 (f) The remedies provided in this Article are cumulative and do not affect the availability
32 of other remedies to prevent abduction.
33 "§ 50A-419. Warrant to take physical custody of child.
34 (a) If a petition under this Article contains allegations, and the court finds, that there is a
35 credible risk that the child is imminently likely to be wrongfully removed, the court may issue
36 an ex parte warrant to take physical custody of the child.
37 (b) The respondent on a petition under subsection (a) of this section must be afforded an
38 opportunity to be heard at the earliest possible time after the ex parte warrant is executed, but not
39 later than the end of the next day that the district court is in session unless a hearing on that date
40 is impossible. In that event, the court must hold the hearing on the first possible day that the
41 district court is in session.
42 (c) An ex parte warrant under subsection (a) of this section to take physical custody of a
43 child must do all of the following:
44 (1) Recite the facts upon which a determination of a credible risk of imminent
45 wrongful removal of the child is based.
46 (2) Authorize law enforcement officers to take physical custody of the child
47 without delay.
48 (3) State the date and time for the hearing on the petition.
49 (4) Provide for the safe interim placement of the child pending further order of
50 the court.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 93

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (d) If feasible, before issuing a warrant and before determining the placement of the child
2 after the warrant is executed, the court may order a search of the relevant databases of the
3 National Crime Information Center system and similar databases of this State or another state to
4 determine if either the petitioner or respondent has a history of domestic violence, stalking, or
5 child abuse or neglect.
6 (e) The petition and warrant must be served on the respondent when, or as soon as
7 possible after, the child is taken into physical custody.
8 (f) A warrant to take physical custody of a child, issued by this State or another state, is
9 enforceable throughout this State. If the court finds that a less intrusive remedy will not be
10 effective, it may authorize law enforcement officers to enter private property to take physical
11 custody of the child, which may include forcible entry at any hour.
12 (g) If the court finds, after a hearing, that a petitioner sought an ex parte warrant under
13 subsection (a) of this section for the purpose of harassment or in bad faith, the court may award
14 the respondent reasonable attorneys' fees, costs, and expenses.
15 (h) This Article does not affect the availability of relief allowed under other State law.
16 "§ 50A-420. Duration of abduction prevention order.
17 An abduction prevention order remains in effect until the earliest of the following:
18 (1) The time stated in the order.
19 (2) The emancipation of the child.
20 (3) The child's attaining 18 years of age.
21 (4) The time the order is modified, revoked, vacated, or superseded by a court
22 with jurisdiction under G.S. 50A-201 through G.S. 50A-203.
23 "§ 50A-421. Uniformity of application and construction.
24 In applying and construing this Article, consideration must be given to the need to promote
25 uniformity of the law with respect to its subject matter among states that enact the Uniform Child
26 Abduction Prevention Act.
27 "§ 50A-422. Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.
28 This Article modifies, limits, and supersedes the federal Electronic Signatures in Global and
29 National Commerce Act, Chapter 96 of Title 15 of the United States Code, but does not modify,
30 limit, or supersede section 101(c) of the act, 15 U.S.C. § 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery
31 of any of the notices described in section 103(b) of the act, 15 U.S.C. § 7003(b)."
32 SECTION 45.(c) The Revisor of Statutes shall cause to be printed, as annotations to
33 the published General Statutes, all relevant portions of the Official Comments to the Uniform
34 Child Abduction Prevention Act and all explanatory comments of the drafters of this section as
35 the Revisor may deem appropriate.
36 SECTION 45.(d) This section becomes effective October 1, 2025, and applies to
37 petitions filed or motions made on or after that date.

39 PART V. ARTICLE THREE OF THE UNIFORM UNREGULATED CHILD CUSTODY
40 TRANSFER ACT
41 SECTION 46.(a) Article 3 of Chapter 48 of the General Statutes is amended by
42 adding a new Part to read:
43 "Part 2A. Information and Guidance.
44 "§ 48-3-230. Title and purpose.
45 This Part consists of and may be cited as the Information and Guidance Provisions of the
46 Uniform Unregulated Child Custody Transfer Act. The purpose of this Part is to prevent the
47 unlawful transfer of custody of minors, as prohibited by G.S. 14-321.2, by better preparing
48 adoptive parents for issues that may arise when caring for an adopted minor.
49 "§ 48-3-231. Definitions.
50 For the purposes of this Part, the following definitions apply:
Page 94 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (1) Intercountry adoption. – An adoption or placement for adoption of a minor
2 who resides in a foreign country at the time of adoption or placement. The
3 term includes an adoption finalized in the minor's country of residence or in a
4 state.
5 (2) Parent. – An individual recognized as a parent under other law of this State.
6 (3) Prospective adoptive parent. – An individual approved or permitted under
7 other law of this State to adopt a minor.
8 (4) Record. – Information inscribed on a tangible medium or stored in an
9 electronic or other medium and retrievable in perceivable form.
10 "§ 48-3-232. Scope.
11 This Part applies to placement for adoption of a minor to whom any of the following applies:
12 (1) Has been or is in foster or institutional care.
13 (2) Previously has been adopted in a state.
14 (3) Has been or is being adopted under the law of a foreign country.
15 (4) Has come or is coming to a state from a foreign country to be adopted.
16 (5) Is not a citizen of the United States.
17 "§ 48-3-233. General adoption information.
18 Within a reasonable time before an agency places a minor for adoption with a prospective
19 adoptive parent, the agency shall provide or cause to be provided to the prospective adoptive
20 parent general adoption information. The information shall address all of the following:
21 (1) Possible physical, mental, emotional, and behavioral issues concerning all of
22 the following:
23 a. Identity, loss, and trauma that a minor might experience before,
24 during, or after adoption.
25 b. A minor leaving familiar ties and surroundings.
26 (2) The effect that access to resources, including health insurance, may have on
27 the ability of an adoptive parent to meet the needs of a minor.
28 (3) Causes of disruption of an adoptive placement or dissolution of an adoption
29 and resources available to help avoid disruption or dissolution.
30 (4) Criminal prohibitions under G.S. 14-321.2.
31 "§ 48-3-234. Nonidentifying information about minor.
32 (a) Within a reasonable time before an agency places a minor to whom this Part applies
33 for adoption with a prospective adoptive parent, the agency shall provide or cause to be provided
34 to the prospective adoptive parent nonidentifying information specific to the minor, in addition
35 to information provided pursuant to G.S. 48-3-205, that is known to or reasonably obtainable by
36 the agency and material to the prospective adoptive parent's informed decision to adopt the minor.
37 To the extent that it is not already being provided under G.S. 48-3-205, the nonidentifying
38 information shall include all of the following:
39 (1) The minor's family, cultural, racial, religious, ethnic, linguistic, and
40 educational background.
41 (2) The minor's physical, mental, emotional, and behavioral health.
42 (3) Circumstances that might adversely affect the minor's physical, mental,
43 emotional, or behavioral health.
44 (4) The minor's medical history, including immunizations.
45 (5) The medical history of the minor's biological parents and siblings.
46 (6) The history of an adoptive or out-of-home placement of the minor and the
47 reason the adoption or placement ended.
48 (7) The minor's United States immigration status.
49 (8) Medical, therapeutic, and educational resources, including
50 language-acquisition training, available to the adoptive parent and minor after
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 95

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 placement for adoption or adoption to assist in responding effectively to
2 physical, mental, emotional, or behavioral health issues.
3 (b) Subject to the requirements of Article 9 of this Chapter, an agency shall include
4 available records relevant to the information in subdivisions (1) through (8) of subsection (a) of
5 this section when providing the information, regardless of whether the information is provided
6 pursuant to subsection (a) of this section or G.S. 48-3-205.
7 (c) If, before an adoption is finalized, additional information under subsection (a) of this
8 section that is material to a prospective adoptive parent's informed decision to adopt the minor
9 becomes known to or reasonably obtainable by the agency, the agency shall provide the
10 information to the prospective adoptive parent.
11 (d) If, after an adoption is finalized, additional information under subsection (a) of this
12 section becomes known to the agency, the agency shall make a reasonable effort to provide the
13 information to the adoptive parent.
14 "§ 48-3-235. Guidance and instruction.
15 (a) An agency placing a minor for adoption shall provide or cause to be provided to the
16 prospective adoptive parent guidance and instruction specific to the minor to help prepare the
17 parent to respond effectively to needs of the minor that are known to or reasonably ascertainable
18 by the agency.
19 (b) The guidance and instruction under subsection (a) of this section shall address, if
20 applicable, all of the following:
21 (1) The potential effect on the minor of all of the following:
22 a. A previous adoption or out-of-home placement.
23 b. Multiple previous adoptions or out-of-home placements.
24 c. Trauma, insecure attachment, fetal alcohol exposure, or malnutrition.
25 d. Neglect, abuse, drug exposure, or similar adversity.
26 e. Separation from a sibling or significant caregiver.
27 f. A difference in ethnicity, race, or cultural identity between the minor
28 and the prospective adoptive parent or other minor of the parent.
29 (2) Information available from the federal government on the process for the
30 minor to acquire United States citizenship.
31 (3) Any other matter the agency considers material to the adoption.
32 (c) The guidance and instruction under subsection (a) of this section shall be provided as
33 follows:
34 (1) For adoption of a minor residing in the United States, a reasonable time before
35 the adoption is finalized.
36 (2) For an intercountry adoption, in accordance with federal law.
37 "§ 48-3-236. Information about financial assistance and support services.
38 Consistent with the purposes of G.S. 48-1-110, on request of a minor who was placed for
39 adoption or the minor's adoptive parent, the agency placing the minor or the Department of Health
40 and Human Services shall provide information about how to obtain financial assistance or
41 support services as follows:
42 (1) To assist the minor or parent to respond effectively to adjustment, behavioral
43 health, and other challenges.
44 (2) To help preserve the placement or adoption.
45 "§ 48-3-237. Agency compliance.
46 (a) The Department of Health and Human Services may investigate an allegation that an
47 agency has failed to comply with this Part and may commence an action for injunctive or other
48 relief or initiate an administrative proceeding against the agency to enforce this Part.
49 (b) The Department of Health and Human Services may initiate a proceeding to
50 determine whether an agency has failed to comply with this Part. If the Department of Health
Page 96 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 and Human Services finds that the agency has failed to comply, the Department may suspend or
2 revoke the agency's license or take other action permitted by law of this State.
3 "§ 48-3-238. Uniformity of application and construction.
4 In applying and construing this Part, a court shall consider the promotion of uniformity of the
5 law among jurisdictions that enact Article 3 of the Uniform Unregulated Child Custody Transfer
6 Act.
7 "§ 48-3-239. Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.
8 This Part modifies, limits, or supersedes the Electronic Signatures in Global and National
9 Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. § 7001 et seq., but does not modify, limit, or supersede 15 U.S.C. §
10 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices described in 15 U.S.C. § 7003(b)."

34 also include an account of the prenatal and postnatal care received by the minor. The information
35 described in this subsection, if known, shall, upon written request of the minor, be made available
36 to the minor upon the minor reaching age 18 or upon the minor's marriage or emancipation.

38 derived from such the information, may shall not be used against the provider or against an
39 individual described in subsection (a) of this section who is the subject of the information in any
40 criminal action or any civil action for damages. In addition, information provided under this
41 section may shall not be admitted in evidence against the provider or against an individual
42 described in subsection (a) of this section who is the subject of the information in any other action
43 or proceeding.
44 (c) The agency placing the minor shall receive and preserve any additional health-related
45 information obtained after the preparation of the document described in subsection (a) of this
46 section.
47 (d) The Division shall develop and make available forms designed to collect the
48 information described in subsection (a) of this section. However, forms reasonably equivalent to
49 those provided by the Division may be substituted."

11 PART VI. CONVEYANCES BETWEEN SPOUSES
12 SECTION 47.(a) G.S. 29-30(a), as amended by Section 1(b) of this act, reads as
13 rewritten:
14 "(a) Except as provided in this subsection, in lieu of the intestate share provided in
15 G.S. 29-14 or G.S. 29-21, or of the elective share provided in G.S. 30-3.1, the surviving spouse
16 of an intestate or the surviving spouse who has petitioned for an elective share is entitled to take
17 as the surviving spouse's intestate share or elective share a life estate in one third in value of all
18 the real estate of which the deceased spouse was seised and possessed of an estate of inheritance
19 at any time during the marriage. The surviving spouse is not entitled to take a life estate in any
20 of the following circumstances:
21 (1) The surviving spouse has waived the surviving spouse's rights by joining with
22 the other spouse in a conveyance of the real estate.
23 (1a) The surviving spouse has waived the right to take a life estate in lieu of an
24 intestate or elective share by an express written waiver.
25 (2) The surviving spouse has waived, released, or conveyed the surviving spouse's
26 interest in the real estate in accordance with G.S. 52-10.
27 (2a) The surviving spouse has conveyed the surviving spouse's interest in the real
28 estate to the other spouse pursuant to G.S. 39-13.3 or G.S. 41-63(4) and has
29 expressly waived or released the surviving spouse's right to take a life estate
30 in the real estate in the instrument of conveyance.
31 (3) The surviving spouse was not required by law to join in a conveyance of the
32 real estate in order to bar the elective life estate.
33 (3a) The surviving spouse has executed a written declaration permitting the
34 deceased spouse to convey or encumber the real estate without the consent or
35 joinder of the surviving spouse.
36 (3b) The real estate in which the deceased spouse had an interest was either
37 apportioned to or sold to another person in a partition proceeding initiated
38 before the deceased spouse's death.
39 (4) The surviving spouse is otherwise not legally entitled to the election provided
40 in this section."

36 PART VII. UNIFORM COMMUNITY PROPERTY DISPOSITION AT DEATH ACT
37 SECTION 50. Chapter 31C of the General Statutes is repealed.
38 SECTION 51. Chapter 30 of the General Statutes is amended by adding a new
39 Article to read:
40 "Article 5.
41 "Uniform Community Property Disposition at Death Act.
42 "§ 30-41. Title.
43 This Article may be cited as the Uniform Community Property Disposition at Death Act.
44 "§ 30-42. Definitions.
45 In this Article, the following definitions apply:
46 (1) Community-property spouse. – An individual in a marriage or other
47 relationship that satisfies all of the following:
48 a. Community property could be acquired under the relationship.
49 b. The relationship remains in existence at the time of death of either
50 party to the relationship.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 103

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (2) Electronic. – Relating to technology having electrical, digital, magnetic,
2 wireless, optical, electromagnetic, or similar capabilities.
3 (3) Jurisdiction. – The United States, a state, a foreign country, or a political
4 subdivision of a foreign country.
5 (4) Partition. – Voluntarily divide property to which this Article otherwise would
6 apply.
7 (5) Person. – Defined in G.S. 28A-1-1.
8 (6) Personal representative. – Defined in G.S. 28A-1-1.
9 (7) Property. – Defined in G.S. 32C-1-102.
10 (8) Reclassify. – To change the characterization or treatment of community
11 property to property owned separately by community-property spouses.
12 (9) Record. – Information inscribed on a tangible medium or stored in an
13 electronic or other medium and retrievable in perceivable form.
14 (10) Sign. – With present intent to authenticate or adopt a record, to do either of
15 the following:
16 a. Execute or adopt a tangible symbol.
17 b. Attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic symbol,
18 sound, or process.
19 (11) State. – Consists of the following:
20 a. A state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the
21 United States Virgin Islands, or any other territory or insular
22 possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
23 b. An Indian tribe or band or Alaskan native village that is recognized by
24 federal law or formally acknowledged by an entity listed in
25 sub-subdivision a. of this subdivision.
26 "§ 30-43. Included and excluded property.
27 (a) Subject to subsection (b) of this section, this Article applies to all of the following
28 property of a community-property spouse, without regard to how the property is titled or held:
29 (1) If a decedent was domiciled in this State at the time of death, all of the
30 following property:
31 a. All or a proportionate part of each item of personal property, wherever
32 located, that was community property under the law of the jurisdiction
33 where the decedent or the surviving community-property spouse was
34 domiciled either when the community property was acquired or, after
35 acquisition, became community property.
36 b. Income, rent, profit, appreciation, or other increase derived from or
37 traceable to property described in sub-subdivision a. of this
38 subdivision.
39 c. Personal property traceable to property described in sub-subdivision a.
40 or b. of this subdivision.
41 (2) Regardless of whether a decedent was domiciled in this State at the time of
42 death, all of the following property:
43 a. All or a proportionate part of each item of real property located in this
44 State traceable to community property or acquired with community
45 property under the law of the jurisdiction where the decedent or the
46 surviving community-property spouse was domiciled either when the
47 community property was acquired or, after acquisition, became
48 community property.
49 b. Income, rent, profit, appreciation, or other increase, derived from or
50 traceable to property described in sub-subdivision a. of this
51 subdivision.
Page 104 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (b) If community-property spouses acquired community property by complying with the
2 law of a jurisdiction that allows for creation of community property by transfer of property to a
3 trust, this Article applies to the property only to the extent the property is held in the trust or
4 characterized as community property by the terms of the trust or the law of the jurisdiction under
5 which the trust was created.
6 (c) This Article does not apply to the following property:
7 (1) Property that community-property spouses have partitioned or reclassified.
8 (2) Property that is the subject of a waiver of rights granted by this Article.
9 "§ 30-44. Form of partition, reclassification, or waiver.
10 (a) Community-property spouses domiciled in this State may partition or reclassify
11 property to which this Article otherwise would apply. The partition or reclassification must be in
12 a record signed by both community-property spouses. Unless both community-property spouses
13 agree otherwise, partition of community property is presumed to result in each spouse owning a
14 one-half separate property interest in each item of property addressed in the record.
15 (b) A community-property spouse domiciled in this State may waive a right granted by
16 this Article only by complying with the law of this State, including this State's choice-of-law
17 rules, applicable to waiver of a spousal property right.
18 "§ 30-45. Community property presumption.
19 This Article is presumed to apply to all property acquired by a community-property spouse
20 when domiciled in a jurisdiction where property acquired by the community-property spouse was
21 presumed to be community property under the law of that jurisdiction. This presumption may be
22 rebutted by a preponderance of the evidence.
23 "§ 30-46. Disposition of property at death.
24 (a) One-half of the property to which this Article applies belongs to the surviving
25 community-property spouse of a decedent and is not subject to disposition by the decedent at
26 death.
27 (b) One-half of the property to which this Article applies belongs to the decedent and is
28 subject to disposition by the decedent at death.
29 (c) The property that belongs to the decedent under subsection (b) of this section is not
30 subject to the surviving community-property spouse's right to petition for an elective share under
31 Article 1A of this Chapter or the surviving community-property spouse's right to elect a life estate
32 under Article 8 of Chapter 29 of the General Statutes.
33 (d) This section does not apply to property transferred by right of survivorship or under
34 a revocable trust or other nonprobate transfer.
35 (e) This section does not limit the right of a surviving community-property spouse to the
36 year's allowance under Article 4 of this Chapter or the property exemptions under Article X of
37 the North Carolina Constitution and Article 16 of Chapter 1C of the General Statutes.
38 (f) If at death a decedent purports to transfer to a third person property that, under this
39 section, belongs to the surviving community-property spouse and transfers other property to the
40 surviving community-property spouse, this section does not limit the authority of the court under
41 other laws of this State to require that the community-property spouse elect between retaining
42 the property transferred to the community-property spouse or asserting rights under this Article.
43 "§ 30-47. Other remedies available at death.
44 (a) At the death of a community-property spouse, the surviving community-property
45 spouse or a personal representative, heir, or nonprobate transferee of the decedent may assert a
46 right based on either of the following acts:
47 (1) An act of the surviving community-property spouse or decedent during the
48 marriage or other relationship under which community property then could be
49 acquired.
50 (2) An act of the decedent that takes effect at the death of the decedent.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 105

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (b) In determining a right under subsection (a) of this section and corresponding remedy,
2 the court shall apply equitable principles and may consider the community property law of the
3 jurisdiction where the decedent or surviving community-property spouse was domiciled when
4 the property was acquired or enhanced.
5 "§ 30-48. Right of surviving community-property spouse.
6 (a) The surviving community-property spouse of a decedent may assert a claim for relief
7 with respect to a right under this Article in accordance with the following:
8 (1) With respect to a claim for relief asserting a right in or to property, the
9 surviving community-property spouse must do either of the following:
10 a. Within one year of the decedent's date of death, commence a civil
11 action in superior court against an heir, devisee, or nonprobate
12 transferee that is in possession of the property.
13 b. Within six months after the issuance of letters testamentary or letters
14 of administration in connection with the decedent's testate or intestate
15 proceeding, file a petition with the clerk of superior court or
16 commence a civil action in superior court in the county in which the
17 primary administration of the decedent's estate lies. A petition with the
18 clerk of superior court shall be filed as an estate proceeding, and the
19 proceeding shall be conducted in accordance with the procedures of
20 Article 2 of Chapter 28A of the General Statutes.
21 (2) With respect to a claim for relief other than a claim under subdivision (a)(1)
22 of this section, the surviving community-property spouse must do either of the
23 following:
24 a. If a personal representative of the decedent's estate is not appointed,
25 commence a civil action in superior court within one year of the
26 decedent's date of death.
27 b. Satisfy the procedural requirements of sub-subdivision (a)(1)b. of this
28 section.
29 (3) The incapacity of the surviving spouse does not toll the time for commencing
30 an action or filing a petition as provided in this section.
31 (b) Unless a timely demand is made under sub-subdivision (a)(1)b. or (a)(2)b. of this
32 section, the personal representative may distribute the assets of the decedent's estate without
33 personal liability for a community-property spouse's claim under this Article.
34 "§ 30-49. Right of heir, devisee, or nonprobate transferee.
35 An heir, devisee, or nonprobate transferee of a deceased community-property spouse may
36 assert a claim for relief with respect to a right under this Article in accordance with the following:
37 (1) With respect to a claim asserting a right in or to property, the heir, devisee, or
38 nonprobate transferee must do either of the following:
39 a. Within one year of the decedent's date of death, commence a civil
40 action in superior court against the surviving community-property
41 spouse who is in possession of the property.
42 b. Satisfy the procedural requirements of G.S. 30-48(a)(1)b.
43 (2) With respect to a claim for relief other than a claim under subdivision (1) of
44 this section, the heir, devisee, or nonprobate transferee must do either of the
45 following:
46 a. If a personal representative of the decedent's estate is not appointed,
47 commence a civil action in superior court within one year of the
48 decedent's date of death.
49 b. Satisfy the procedural requirements of G.S. 30-48(a)(1)b.
50 (3) The incapacity of the heir, devisee, or nonprobate transferee does not toll the
51 time for commencing an action or filing a petition as provided in this section.

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 "§ 30-50. Protection of third person.
2 (a) With respect to property to which this Article applies, a person is not liable under this
3 Article if all of the following apply:
4 (1) The person transacts in good faith and for value with either of the following:
5 a. A community-property spouse.
6 b. After the death of the decedent, a surviving community-property
7 spouse, personal representative, heir, devisee, or nonprobate transferee
8 of the decedent.
9 (2) The person does not know or have reason to know that the other party to the
10 transaction is exceeding or improperly exercising the party's authority.
11 (b) Good faith under subdivision (a)(1) of this section does not require the person to
12 inquire into the extent or propriety of the exercise of authority by the other party to the
13 transaction.
14 (c) With respect to real property to which this Article applies, a lien creditor or a
15 purchaser for value of the property is not liable under this Article unless, before the lien was
16 acquired or the purchase was made, the community-property spouses gave notice in a registered
17 instrument of their intention for this Article to apply to the property. Priority among this
18 registered instrument and other registered instruments is governed by G.S. 47-18.
19 "§ 30-51. Principles of law and equity.
20 The principles of law and equity supplement this Article except to the extent inconsistent
21 with this Article.
22 "§ 30-52. Uniformity of application and construction.
23 In applying and construing this Article, a court shall consider the promotion of uniformity of
24 the law among jurisdictions that enact the Uniform Community Property Disposition at Death
25 Act."

11 SECTION 53. If a provision of this Part or its application to a person or circumstance
12 is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect another provision or application that can be given
13 effect without the invalid provision.
14 SECTION 54. The Revisor of Statutes shall cause to be printed, as annotations to
15 the published General Statutes, all relevant portions of the Official Comments to the Uniform
16 Community Property Disposition at Death Act and all explanatory comments of the drafters of
17 this Part as the Revisor may deem appropriate.
18 SECTION 55. If a right with respect to property to which this act applies is acquired,
19 extinguished, or barred on the expiration of a limitation period that began to run under another
20 statute before the effective date of this Part, that statute continues to apply to the right even if the
21 statute has been repealed or superseded by this Part.
22 SECTION 56. This Part becomes effective January 1, 2026. Except as provided in
23 Section 55 of this act, this act applies to a judicial proceeding commenced on or after that date,
24 regardless of the date of death of the decedent.

28 SUBPART VIII-A. CONTROLLABLE ELECTRONIC RECORDS
29 SECTION 57. Chapter 25 of the General Statutes is amended by adding a new

31 "Article 12.
32 "Controllable Electronic Records.
33 "§ 25-12-101. Title.
34 This Article may be cited as Uniform Commercial Code – Controllable Electronic Records.
35 "§ 25-12-102. Definitions.
36 (a) Article 12 Definitions. – In this Article, the following definitions apply:
37 (1) Account debtor. – Defined in G.S. 25-9-102.
38 (2) Chattel paper. – Defined in G.S. 25-9-102.
39 (3) Controllable account. – Defined in G.S. 25-9-102.
40 (4) Controllable electronic record. – A record stored in an electronic medium that
41 can be subjected to control under G.S. 25-12-105. The term does not include
42 a controllable account, a controllable payment intangible, a deposit account,
43 an electronic copy of a record evidencing chattel paper, an electronic
44 document of title, electronic money, investment property, or a transferable
45 record.
46 (5) Controllable payment intangible. – Defined in G.S. 25-9-102.
47 (6) Deposit account. – Defined in G.S. 25-9-102.
48 (7) Electronic money. – Defined in G.S. 25-9-102.
49 (8) Investment property. – Defined in G.S. 25-9-102.
50 (9) Qualifying purchaser. – A purchaser of a controllable electronic record or an
51 interest in a controllable electronic record that obtains control of the
Page 108 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 controllable electronic record for value, in good faith, and without notice of a
2 claim of a property right in the controllable electronic record.
3 (10) Transferable record. – Has the meaning provided for that term in either of the
4 following:
5 a. Section 201(a)(1) of the Electronic Signatures in Global and National
6 Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. § 7021(a)(1).
7 b. G.S. 66-326(a).
8 (11) Value. – Has the meaning provided in G.S. 25-3-303(a), as if references in
9 that subsection to an "instrument" were references to a controllable account,
10 controllable electronic record, or controllable payment intangible.
11 (b) Article 1 Definitions and Principles. – Article 1 of this Chapter contains general
12 definitions and principles of construction and interpretation applicable throughout this Article.
13 "§ 25-12-103. Relation to Article 9 and consumer laws.
14 (a) Article 9 Governs in Case of Conflict. – If there is conflict between this Article and
15 Article 9 of this Chapter, Article 9 of this Chapter governs.
16 (b) Applicable Consumer Law and Other Laws. – A transaction subject to this Article is
17 subject to any applicable rule of law that establishes a different rule for consumers, to any other
18 statute or rule of this State that regulates the rates, charges, agreements, and practices for loans,
19 credit sales, or other extensions of credit, and to any consumer-protection statute or rule of this
20 State, including Chapter 24 of the General Statutes, the Retail Installment Sales Act (Chapter
21 25A of the General Statutes), the North Carolina Consumer Finance Act (Article 15 of Chapter
22 53 of the General Statutes), and the Pawnbrokers and Currency Converters Modernization Act
23 (Part 1 of Article 45 of Chapter 66 of the General Statutes).
24 "§ 25-12-104. Rights in controllable account, controllable electronic record, and
25 controllable payment intangible.
26 (a) Applicability of Section to Controllable Account and Controllable Payment
27 Intangible. – This section applies to the acquisition and purchase of rights in a controllable
28 account or controllable payment intangible, including the rights and benefits under subsections
29 (c), (d), (e), (g), and (h) of this section of a purchaser and qualifying purchaser, in the same
30 manner this section applies to a controllable electronic record.
31 (b) Control of Controllable Account and Controllable Payment Intangible. – To
32 determine whether a purchaser of a controllable account or a controllable payment intangible is
33 a qualifying purchaser, the purchaser obtains control of the account or payment intangible if it
34 obtains control of the controllable electronic record that evidences the account or payment
35 intangible.
36 (c) Applicability of Other Law to Acquisition of Rights. – Except as provided in this
37 section, law other than this Article determines whether a person acquires a right in a controllable
38 electronic record and the right the person acquires.
39 (d) Shelter Principle and Purchase of Limited Interest. – A purchaser of a controllable
40 electronic record acquires all rights in the controllable electronic record that the transferor had or
41 had power to transfer, except that a purchaser of a limited interest in a controllable electronic
42 record acquires rights only to the extent of the interest purchased.
43 (e) Rights of Qualifying Purchaser. – A qualifying purchaser acquires its rights in the
44 controllable electronic record free of a claim of a property right in the controllable electronic
45 record.
46 (f) Limitation of Rights of Qualifying Purchaser in Other Property. – Except as provided
47 in subsections (a) and (e) of this section for a controllable account and a controllable payment
48 intangible or law other than this Article, a qualifying purchaser takes a right to payment, right to
49 performance, or other interest in property evidenced by the controllable electronic record subject
50 to a claim of a property right in the right to payment, right to performance, or other interest in
51 property.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 109

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (g) No-Action Protection for Qualifying Purchaser. – An action shall not be asserted
2 against a qualifying purchaser based on both a purchase by the qualifying purchaser of a
3 controllable electronic record and a claim of a property right in another controllable electronic
4 record, whether the action is framed in conversion, replevin, constructive trust, equitable lien, or
5 other theory.
6 (h) Filing Not Notice. – Filing of a financing statement under Article 9 of this Chapter is
7 not notice of a claim of a property right in a controllable electronic record.
8 "§ 25-12-105. Control of controllable electronic record.
9 (a) General Rule for Control of Controllable Electronic Record. – A person has control
10 of a controllable electronic record if the electronic record, a record attached to or logically
11 associated with the electronic record, or a system in which the electronic record is recorded does
12 both of the following:
13 (1) Gives the person both of the following:
14 a. Power to avail itself of substantially all the benefit from the electronic
15 record.
16 b. Exclusive power, subject to subsection (b) of this section, to do both
17 of the following:
18 1. Prevent others from availing themselves of substantially all the
19 benefit from the electronic record.
20 2. Transfer control of the electronic record to another person or
21 cause another person to obtain control of another controllable
22 electronic record as a result of the transfer of the electronic
23 record.
24 (2) Enables the person readily to identify itself in any way, including by name,
25 identifying number, cryptographic key, office, or account number, as having
26 the powers specified in subdivision (1) of this subsection.
27 (b) Meaning of Exclusive. – Subject to subsection (c) of this section, a power is exclusive
28 under sub-subdivision (a)(1)b. of this section even if either of the following applies:
29 (1) The controllable electronic record, a record attached to or logically associated
30 with the electronic record, or a system in which the electronic record is
31 recorded limits the use of the electronic record or has a protocol programmed
32 to cause a change, including a transfer or loss of control or a modification of
33 benefits afforded by the electronic record.
34 (2) The power is shared with another person.
35 (c) When Power Not Shared with Another Person. – A power of a person is not shared
36 with another person under subdivision (b)(2) of this section and the person's power is not
37 exclusive if both of the following apply:
38 (1) The person can exercise the power only if the power also is exercised by the
39 other person.
40 (2) Either of the following applies:
41 a. The other person can exercise the power without exercise of the power
42 by the person.
43 b. The other person is the transferor to the person of an interest in the
44 controllable electronic record or a controllable account or controllable
45 payment intangible evidenced by the controllable electronic record.
46 (d) Presumption of Exclusivity of Certain Powers. – If a person has the powers specified
47 in sub-subdivision (a)(1)b. of this section, the powers are presumed to be exclusive.
48 (e) Control Through Another Person. – A person has control of a controllable electronic
49 record if either of the following applies to another person, other than the transferor to the person
50 of an interest in the controllable electronic record or a controllable account or controllable
51 payment intangible evidenced by the controllable electronic record:
Page 110 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (1) The other person has control of the electronic record and acknowledges that it
2 has control on behalf of the person.
3 (2) The other person obtains control of the electronic record after having
4 acknowledged that it will obtain control of the electronic record on behalf of
5 the person.
6 (f) No Requirement to Acknowledge. – A person that has control under this section is
7 not required to acknowledge that it has control on behalf of another person.
8 (g) No Duties or Confirmation. – If a person acknowledges that it has or will obtain
9 control on behalf of another person, unless the person otherwise agrees or law other than this
10 Article or Article 9 of this Chapter otherwise provides, the person does not owe any duty to the
11 other person and is not required to confirm the acknowledgment to any other person.
12 "§ 25-12-106. Discharge of account debtor on controllable account or controllable payment
13 intangible.
14 (a) Discharge of Account Debtor. – An account debtor on a controllable account or
15 controllable payment intangible may discharge its obligation by paying either of the following
16 persons:
17 (1) The person having control of the controllable electronic record that evidences
18 the controllable account or controllable payment intangible.
19 (2) Except as provided in subsection (b) of this section, a person that formerly had
20 control of the controllable electronic record.
21 (b) Content and Effect of Notification. – Subject to subsection (d) of this section, the
22 account debtor shall not discharge its obligation by paying a person that formerly had control of
23 the controllable electronic record if the account debtor receives a notification that satisfies all of
24 the following requirements:
25 (1) The notification is signed by a person that formerly had control or the person
26 to which control was transferred.
27 (2) The notification reasonably identifies the controllable account or controllable
28 payment intangible.
29 (3) The notification notifies the account debtor that control of the controllable
30 electronic record that evidences the controllable account or controllable
31 payment intangible was transferred.
32 (4) The notification identifies the transferee, in any reasonable way, including by
33 name, identifying number, cryptographic key, office, or account number.
34 (5) The notification provides a commercially reasonable method by which the
35 account debtor is to pay the transferee.
36 (c) Discharge Following Effective Notification. – After receipt of a notification that
37 complies with subsection (b) of this section, the account debtor may discharge its obligation by
38 paying in accordance with the notification and shall not discharge the obligation by paying a
39 person that formerly had control.
40 (d) When Notification Ineffective. – Subject to subsection (h) of this section, all of the
41 following apply to a notification under subsection (b) of this section:
42 (1) The notification is ineffective unless, before the notification is sent, the
43 account debtor and the person that, at that time, had control of the controllable
44 electronic record that evidences the controllable account or controllable
45 payment intangible agree in a signed record to a commercially reasonable
46 method by which a person may furnish reasonable proof that control has been
47 transferred.
48 (2) The notification is ineffective to the extent an agreement between the account
49 debtor and seller of a payment intangible limits the account debtor's duty to
50 pay a person other than the seller and the limitation is effective under law
51 other than this Article.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 111

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (3) The notification is ineffective at the option of the account debtor, if the
2 notification notifies the account debtor to do any of the following:
3 a. Divide a payment.
4 b. Make less than the full amount of an installment or other periodic
5 payment.
6 c. Pay any part of a payment by more than one method or to more than
7 one person.
8 (e) Proof of Transfer of Control. – Subject to subsection (h) of this section, if requested
9 by the account debtor, the person giving the notification under subsection (b) of this section
10 seasonably shall furnish reasonable proof, using the method in the agreement referred to in
11 subdivision (d)(1) of this section, that control of the controllable electronic record has been
12 transferred. Unless the person complies with the request, the account debtor may discharge its
13 obligation by paying a person that formerly had control, even if the account debtor has received
14 a notification under subsection (b) of this section.
15 (f) What Constitutes Reasonable Proof. – A person furnishes reasonable proof under
16 subsection (e) of this section that control has been transferred if the person demonstrates, using
17 the method in the agreement referred to in subdivision (d)(1) of this section, that the transferee
18 has the power to do all of the following:
19 (1) Avail itself of substantially all the benefit from the controllable electronic
20 record.
21 (2) Prevent others from availing themselves of substantially all the benefit from
22 the controllable electronic record.
23 (3) Transfer the powers specified in subdivisions (1) and (2) of this subsection to
24 another person.
25 (g) Rights Not Waivable. – Subject to subsection (h) of this section, an account debtor
26 shall not waive or vary its rights under subdivision (d)(1) and subsection (e) of this section or its
27 option under subdivision (d)(3) of this section.
28 (h) Rule for Individual Under Other Law. – This section is subject to law other than this
29 Article that establishes a different rule for an account debtor who is an individual and who
30 incurred the obligation primarily for personal, family, or household purposes.
31 "§ 25-12-107. Governing law.
32 (a) General Rule for Governing Law. – Except as provided in subsection (b) of this
33 section, the local law of a controllable electronic record's jurisdiction governs a matter covered
34 by this Article.
35 (b) Governing Law for G.S. 25-12-106. – For a controllable electronic record that
36 evidences a controllable account or controllable payment intangible, the local law of the
37 controllable electronic record's jurisdiction governs a matter covered by G.S. 25-12-106 unless
38 an effective agreement determines that the local law of another jurisdiction governs.
39 (c) Controllable Electronic Record's Jurisdiction. – The following rules determine a
40 controllable electronic record's jurisdiction under this section:
41 (1) If the controllable electronic record, or a record attached to or logically
42 associated with the controllable electronic record and readily available for
43 review, expressly provides that a particular jurisdiction is the controllable
44 electronic record's jurisdiction for purposes of this Article or Chapter, that
45 jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record's jurisdiction.
46 (2) If subdivision (1) of this subsection does not apply and the rules of the system
47 in which the controllable electronic record is recorded are readily available for
48 review and expressly provide that a particular jurisdiction is the controllable
49 electronic record's jurisdiction for purposes of this Article or Chapter, that
50 jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record's jurisdiction.
Page 112 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (3) If subdivisions (1) and (2) of this subsection do not apply and the controllable
2 electronic record, or a record attached to or logically associated with the
3 controllable electronic record and readily available for review, expressly
4 provides that the controllable electronic record is governed by the law of a
5 particular jurisdiction, that jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record's
6 jurisdiction.
7 (4) If subdivisions (1), (2), and (3) of this subsection do not apply and the rules
8 of the system in which the controllable electronic record is recorded are
9 readily available for review and expressly provide that the controllable
10 electronic record or the system is governed by the law of a particular
11 jurisdiction, that jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record's jurisdiction.
12 (5) If subdivisions (1) through (4) of this subsection do not apply, the controllable
13 electronic record's jurisdiction is the District of Columbia.
14 (d) Applicability of Article 12. – If subdivision (c)(5) of this section applies and Article
15 12 is not in effect in the District of Columbia without material modification, the governing law
16 for a matter covered by this Article is the law of the District of Columbia as though Article 12
17 were in effect in the District of Columbia without material modification. In this subsection,
18 "Article 12" means Article 12 of Uniform Commercial Code Amendments (2022).
19 (e) Relation of Matter or Transaction to Controllable Electronic Record's Jurisdiction Not
20 Necessary. – To the extent subsections (a) and (b) of this section provide that the local law of the
21 controllable electronic record's jurisdiction governs a matter covered by this Article, that law
22 governs even if the matter or a transaction to which the matter relates does not bear any relation
23 to the controllable electronic record's jurisdiction.
24 (f) Rights of Purchasers Determined at Time of Purchase. – The rights acquired under
25 G.S. 25-12-104 by a purchaser or qualifying purchaser are governed by the law applicable under
26 this section at the time of purchase."
