35 SECTION 60. G.S. 25-9-105 reads as rewritten:
36 "§ 25-9-105. Control of electronic chattel paper.copy of record evidencing chattel paper.
37 (a) General Rule: Control of Electronic Chattel Paper. – A secured party has control of
38 electronic chattel paper if a system employed for evidencing the transfer of interests in the chattel
39 paper reliably establishes the secured party as the person to which the chattel paper was assigned.
40 (b) Specific Facts Giving Control. – A system satisfies subsection (a) of this section if
41 the record or records comprising the chattel paper are created, stored, and assigned in such a
42 manner that:
43 (1) A single authoritative copy of the record or records exists which is unique,
44 identifiable, and, except as otherwise provided in subdivisions (4), (5), and (6)
45 of this section, unalterable;
46 (2) The authoritative copy identifies the secured party as the assignee of the
47 record or records;
48 (3) The authoritative copy is communicated to and maintained by the secured
49 party or its designated custodian;
50 (4) Copies or amendments that add or change an identified assignee of the
51 authoritative copy can be made only with the consent of the secured party;

1 (5) Each copy of the authoritative copy and any copy of a copy is readily
2 identifiable as a copy that is not the authoritative copy; and
3 (6) Any amendment of the authoritative copy is readily identifiable as authorized
4 or unauthorized.
5 (a) General Rule for Control of Electronic Copy of Record Evidencing Chattel Paper. –
6 A purchaser has control of an authoritative electronic copy of a record evidencing chattel paper
7 if a system employed for evidencing the assignment of interests in the chattel paper reliably
8 establishes the purchaser as the person to which the authoritative electronic copy was assigned.
9 (b) Single Authoritative Copy. – A system satisfies subsection (a) of this section if the
10 record or records evidencing the chattel paper are created, stored, and assigned in a manner that
11 satisfies all of the following requirements:

18 or its designated custodian.

21 (5) Each copy of the authoritative copy and any copy of a copy is readily

24 or unauthorized.

32 identifying number, cryptographic key, office, or account number, as the

37 authoritative electronic copy.

40 under subdivision (c)(3) of this section even if either of the following applies:
41 (1) The authoritative electronic copy, a record attached to or logically associated
42 with the authoritative electronic copy, or a system in which the authoritative
43 electronic copy is recorded limits the use of the authoritative electronic copy
44 or has a protocol programmed to cause a change, including a transfer or loss
45 of control.
46 (2) The power is shared with another person.
47 (e) When Power Not Shared with Another Person. – A power of a purchaser is not shared
48 with another person under subdivision (d)(2) of this section and the purchaser's power is not
49 exclusive if both of the following apply:
50 (1) The purchaser can exercise the power only if the power also is exercised by
51 the other person.

32 "§ 25-9-306.1. Law governing perfection and priority of security interests in chattel paper.
33 (a) Chattel Paper Evidenced by Authoritative Electronic Copy. – Except as provided in
34 subsection (d) of this section, if chattel paper is evidenced only by an authoritative electronic
35 copy of the chattel paper or is evidenced by an authoritative electronic copy and an authoritative
36 tangible copy, the local law of the chattel paper's jurisdiction governs perfection, the effect of
37 perfection or nonperfection, and the priority of a security interest in the chattel paper, even if the
38 transaction does not bear any relation to the chattel paper's jurisdiction.
39 (b) Chattel Paper's Jurisdiction. – The following rules determine the chattel paper's
40 jurisdiction under this section:
41 (1) If the authoritative electronic copy of the record evidencing chattel paper, or
42 a record attached to or logically associated with the electronic copy and
43 readily available for review, expressly provides that a particular jurisdiction
44 is the chattel paper's jurisdiction for purposes of this Part, this Article, or this
45 Chapter, that jurisdiction is the chattel paper's jurisdiction.
46 (2) If subdivision (1) of this subsection does not apply and the rules of the system
47 in which the authoritative electronic copy is recorded are readily available for
48 review and expressly provide that a particular jurisdiction is the chattel paper's
49 jurisdiction for purposes of this Part, this Article, or this Chapter, that
50 jurisdiction is the chattel paper's jurisdiction.

1 (3) If subdivisions (1) and (2) of this subsection do not apply and the authoritative

4 chattel paper is governed by the law of a particular jurisdiction, that
5 jurisdiction is the chattel paper's jurisdiction.

26 and (b) of this section do not apply to limit the liability of a secured party to a person if, at the
27 time the secured party obtains control of collateral that is a controllable account, controllable
28 electronic record, or controllable payment intangible or at the time the security interest attaches
29 to the collateral, whichever is later, both of the following apply:
30 (1) The person is a debtor or obligor.
31 (2) The secured party knows that the information in sub-subdivision (b)(1)a., b.,
32 or c. of this section relating to the person is not provided by the collateral, a
33 record attached to or logically associated with the collateral, or the system in
34 which the collateral is recorded."

38 SECTION 115. G.S. 25-2-106 reads as rewritten:
39 "§ 25-2-106. Definitions: "Contract"; "agreement"; "contract for sale"; "sale"; "present
40 sale"; "layaway contract"; "conforming" to contract; "termination";
41 "cancellation.""cancellation"; "hybrid transaction."
42 (1)(a) In this article unless the context otherwise requires Article, "contract" and
43 "agreement" are limited to those relating to the present or future sale of goods, including layaway
44 contracts. "Contract for sale" includes both a present sale of goods and a contract to sell goods at
45 a future time. A "sale" consists in the passing of title from the seller to the buyer for a price
46 (G.S. 25-2-401). A "present sale" means a sale which that is accomplished by the making of the
47 contract. A "layaway contract" means any contract for the sale of goods in which the seller agrees
48 with the purchaser, in consideration for the purchaser's payment of a deposit, down payment, or
49 similar initial payment, to hold identified goods for future delivery upon the purchaser's payment
50 of a specified additional amount, whether in installments or otherwise.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 175

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (2)(b) Goods or conduct including any part of a performance are "conforming" or conform
2 to the contract when they are in accordance with the obligations under the contract.
3 (3)(c) "Termination" occurs when either party pursuant to a power created by agreement or
4 law puts an end to the contract otherwise than for its breach. On "termination" "termination," all
5 obligations which that are still executory on both sides are discharged discharged, but any right
6 based on prior breach or performance survives.
7 (4)(d) "Cancellation" occurs when either party puts an end to the contract for breach by the
8 other and its effect is the same as that of "termination" except that the cancelling party also retains
9 any remedy for breach of the whole contract or any unperformed balance.
10 (e) "Hybrid transaction" means a single transaction involving a sale of goods and any of
11 the following:
12 (1) The provision of services.
13 (2) A lease of other goods.
14 (3) A sale, lease, or license of property other than goods."

42 this Article that relate primarily to the transaction as a whole do not
43 apply.
44 b. G.S. 25-2A-209 applies if the lease is a finance lease.

48 (2) If the lease-of-goods aspects predominate, this Article applies to the
49 transaction but does not preclude application in appropriate circumstances of

29 "§ 25-3-604. Discharge by cancellation or renunciation.
30 (a) A person entitled to enforce an instrument, with or without consideration, may
31 discharge the obligation of a party to pay the instrument (i) by an intentional voluntary act, such
32 as surrender of the instrument to the party, destruction, mutilation, or cancellation of the
33 instrument, cancellation or striking out of the party's signature, or the addition of words to the
34 instrument indicating discharge, or (ii) by agreeing not to sue or otherwise renouncing rights
35 against the party by a signed writing. The obligation of a party to pay a check is not discharged
36 solely by destruction of the check in connection with a process in which information is extracted
37 from the check and an image of the check is made and, subsequently, the information and image
38 are transmitted for payment.
39 (b) Cancellation or striking out of an endorsement indorsement pursuant to subsection (a)
40 of this section does not affect the status and rights of a party derived from the indorsement."

22 SECTION 134. G.S. 25-4A-201 reads as rewritten:
23 "§ 25-4A-201. Security procedure.
24 "Security procedure" means a procedure established by agreement of a customer and a
25 receiving bank for the purpose of (i) verifying that a payment order or communication amending
26 or cancelling a payment order is that of the customer, or (ii) detecting error in the transmission
27 or the content of the payment order or communication. A security procedure may impose an
28 obligation on the receiving bank or the customer and may require the use of algorithms or other
29 codes, identifying words or words, numbers, symbols, sounds, biometrics, encryption, call-back
30 procedures, or similar security devices. Comparison of a signature on a payment order or
31 communication with an authorized specimen signature of the customer or requiring a payment
32 order to be sent from a known email address, IP address, or telephone number is not by itself a
33 security procedure."

15 GENERAL TRANSITIONAL PROVISION
16 SECTION 154. General Applicability; Saving Clause. – This Part applies to a
17 transaction, lien, or other interest in property that is entered into, created, or acquired on or after
18 the effective date of this act. Except as otherwise provided in this Subpart, a transaction validly
19 entered into before the effective date of this Part and the rights, duties, and interests flowing from
20 the transaction remain valid thereafter and may be terminated, completed, consummated, or
21 enforced as required or permitted by law other than Chapter 25 of the General Statutes or, if
22 applicable, Chapter 25 of the General Statutes, as though this Part had not taken effect.
23
24 TRANSITIONAL PROVISIONS FOR ARTICLES 9 AND 12
25 SECTION 155.(a) Pre-Effective-Date Transaction, Lien, or Interest. – Except as
26 provided in this section, amended Article 9 and Article 12 apply to a transaction, lien, or other
27 interest in property, even if the transaction, lien, or interest was entered into, created, or acquired
28 before the effective date of this Part.
29 SECTION 155.(b) Continuing Validity. – Except as provided in subsections (c)
30 through (j) of this section, both of the following apply:
31 (1) A transaction, lien, or interest in property that was validly entered into,
32 created, or transferred before the effective date of this Part and was not
33 governed by Chapter 25 of the General Statutes, but would be subject to
34 amended Article 9 or Article 12 if it had been entered into, created, or
35 transferred on or after the effective date of this Part, including the rights,
36 duties, and interests flowing from the transaction, lien, or interest, remains
37 valid on and after the effective date of this Part.
38 (2) A transaction, lien, or interest described in subdivision (1) of this subsection
39 may be terminated, completed, consummated, and enforced as required or
40 permitted by this Part or by the law that would apply if this Part had not taken
41 effect.
42 SECTION 155.(c) Pre-Effective-Date Proceeding. – This Part does not affect an
43 action, case, or proceeding commenced before the effective date of this Part.
44 SECTION 155.(d) Security Interest Perfected Before Effective Date. – Both of the
45 following apply to a security interest perfected before the effective date of this Part:
46 (1) A security interest that is enforceable and perfected immediately before the
47 effective date of this Part is a perfected security interest under this Part if, on
48 the effective date of this Part, the requirements for enforceability and
49 perfection under this Part are satisfied without further action.
50 (2) If a security interest is enforceable and perfected immediately before the
51 effective date of this Part, but the requirements for enforceability or perfection
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 199

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 under this Part are not satisfied on the effective date of this Part, all of the
2 following apply to the security interest:
3 a. The security interest is a perfected security interest until the earlier of
4 the time perfection would have ceased under the law in effect
5 immediately before the effective date of this Part or the adjustment
6 date.
7 b. The security interest remains enforceable thereafter only if the security
8 interest satisfies the requirements for enforceability under
9 G.S. 25-9-203, as amended by this Part, before the adjustment date.
10 c. The security interest remains perfected thereafter only if the
11 requirements for perfection under this Part are satisfied before the time
12 specified in sub-subdivision a. of this subdivision.
13 SECTION 155.(e) Security Interest Unperfected Before Effective Date. – All of the
14 following apply to a security interest that is enforceable immediately before the effective date of
15 this Part but is unperfected at that time:
16 (1) The security interest remains an enforceable security interest until the
17 adjustment date.
18 (2) The security interest remains enforceable thereafter if the security interest
19 becomes enforceable under G.S. 25-9-203, as amended by this Part, on the
20 effective date of this Part or before the adjustment date.
21 (3) The security interest becomes perfected at either of the following times:
22 a. Without further action, on the effective date of this Part if the
23 requirements for perfection under this Part are satisfied before or at
24 that time.
25 b. When the requirements for perfection are satisfied if the requirements
26 are satisfied after the effective date of this Part.
27 SECTION 155.(f) Pre-Effective-Date Action; Attachment and Perfection Before
28 Adjustment Date. – If action, other than the filing of a financing statement, is taken before the
29 effective date of this Part and the action would have resulted in perfection of the security interest
30 had the security interest become enforceable before the effective date of this Part, the action is
31 effective to perfect a security interest that attaches under this Part before the adjustment date. An
32 attached security interest becomes unperfected on the adjustment date unless the security interest
33 becomes a perfected security interest under this Part before the adjustment date.
34 SECTION 155.(g) Pre-Effective-Date Filing. – The filing of a financing statement
35 before the effective date of this Part is effective to perfect a security interest on the effective date
36 of this Part to the extent the filing would satisfy the requirements for perfection under this Part.
37 SECTION 155.(h) Pre-Effective-Date Enforceability Action. – The taking of an
38 action before the effective date of this Part is sufficient for the enforceability of a security interest
39 on the effective date of this Part if the action would satisfy the requirements for enforceability
40 under this Part.
41 SECTION 155.(i) Priority. –
42 (1) Determination of priority. – Subject to subdivisions (2) and (3) of this
43 subsection, this Part determines the priority of conflicting claims to collateral.
44 (2) Established priorities. – Subject to subdivision (3) of this subsection, if the
45 priorities of claims to collateral were established before the effective date of
46 this Part, Article 9 of Chapter 25 of the General Statutes as in effect before the
47 effective date of this Part determines priority.
48 (3) Determination of certain priorities on adjustment date. – On the adjustment
49 date, to the extent the priorities determined by amended Article 9 modify the
50 priorities established before the effective date of this Part, the priorities of
Page 200 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 claims to Article 12 property and electronic money established before the
2 effective date of this Part cease to apply.
3 SECTION 155.(j) Priority of Claims When Priority Rules of Article 9 Do Not
4 Apply. –
5 (1) Determination of priority. – Subject to subdivisions (1) and (2) of this
6 subsection, Article 12 determines the priority of conflicting claims to Article
7 12 property when the priority rules of amended Article 9 do not apply.
8 (2) Established priorities. – Subject to subdivision (3) of this subsection, when the
9 priority rules of amended Article 9 do not apply and the priorities of claims to
10 Article 12 property were established before the effective date of this Part, law
11 other than Article 12 determines priority.
12 (3) Determination of certain priorities on adjustment date. – When the priority
13 rules of amended Article 9 do not apply, to the extent the priorities determined
14 by this Part modify the priorities established before the effective date of this
15 Part, the priorities of claims to Article 12 property established before the
16 effective date of this Part cease to apply on the adjustment date.

25 PART IX. UNIFORM SPECIAL DEPOSITS ACT
26 SECTION 158. The General Statutes is amended by adding a new Chapter to read:
27 "Chapter 54D.
28 "Uniform Special Deposits Act.
29 "§ 54D-1. Title.
30 This Chapter may be cited as the Uniform Special Deposits Act.
31 "§ 54D-2. Definitions.
32 In this Chapter, the following definitions apply:
33 (1) Account agreement. – An agreement to which all of the following apply:
34 a. The agreement is in a record between a bank and one or more
35 depositors.
36 b. The agreement may have one or more beneficiaries as additional
37 parties.
38 c. The agreement states the intention of the parties to establish a special
39 deposit governed by this Chapter.
40 (2) Bank. – A person engaged in the business of banking and includes a bank as
41 defined in G.S. 53C-1-4, savings bank, savings and loan association, and
42 credit union. Each branch or separate office of a bank is a separate bank for
43 the purpose of this Chapter.
44 (3) Beneficiary. – A person that satisfies either of the following:
45 a. The person is identified as a beneficiary in an account agreement.
46 b. If not identified as a beneficiary in an account agreement, the person
47 is entitled to payment from a special deposit under the account
48 agreement or on termination of the special deposit.
49 (4) Contingency. – An event or circumstance stated in an account agreement that
50 is not certain to occur but must occur before the bank is obligated to pay a
51 beneficiary.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 201

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (5) Creditor process. – Attachment, garnishment, levy, notice of lien,
2 sequestration, or similar process issued by or on behalf of a creditor or other
3 claimant.
4 (6) Depositor. – A person that establishes or funds a special deposit.
5 (7) Good faith. – Honesty in fact and observance of reasonable commercial
6 standards of fair dealing.
7 (8) "Knowledge" of a fact. – Either of the following:
8 a. With respect to a beneficiary, actual knowledge of the fact.
9 b. With respect to a bank holding a special deposit, either of the
10 following:
11 1. If the bank has established a reasonable routine for
12 communicating material information to an individual to whom
13 the bank has assigned responsibility for the special deposit and
14 maintains reasonable compliance with the routine, actual
15 knowledge of the fact by that individual.
16 2. If the bank has not established and maintained reasonable
17 compliance with a routine described in sub-sub-subdivision 1.
18 of this sub-subdivision, implied knowledge of the fact that
19 would have come to the attention of an individual to whom the
20 bank has assigned responsibility for the special deposit.
21 (9) Obligated to pay a beneficiary. – A beneficiary is entitled under the account
22 agreement to receive from the bank a payment when a contingency has
23 occurred and the bank has knowledge the contingency has occurred.
24 "Obligation to pay a beneficiary" has a corresponding meaning.
25 (10) Permissible purpose. – A governmental, regulatory, commercial, charitable,
26 or testamentary objective of the parties stated in an account agreement. The
27 term includes an objective to do any of the following:
28 a. Hold funds in any of the following circumstances:
29 1. In escrow, including for a purchase and sale, lease, buyback,
30 or other transaction.
31 2. As a security deposit of a tenant.
32 3. That may be distributed to a person as remuneration, retirement
33 or other benefit, or compensation under a judgment, consent
34 decree, court order, or other decision of a tribunal.
35 4. For distribution to a defined class of persons after
36 identification of the class members and their interest in the
37 funds.
38 b. Provide assurance with respect to an obligation created by contract,
39 such as earnest money to ensure a transaction closes.
40 c. Settle an obligation that arises in the operation of a payment system,
41 securities settlement system, or other financial market infrastructure.
42 d. Provide assurance with respect to an obligation that arises in the
43 operation of a payment system, securities settlement system, or other
44 financial market infrastructure.
45 e. Hold margin, other cash collateral, or funds that support the orderly
46 functioning of financial market infrastructure or the performance of an
47 obligation with respect to the infrastructure.
48 (11) Person. – An individual, estate, business or nonprofit entity, government or
49 governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality, or other legal entity.
50 The term includes a protected series, however denominated, of an entity if the
51 protected series is established under law that limits, or limits if conditions
Page 202 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 specified under law are satisfied, the ability of a creditor of the entity or of any
2 other protected series of the entity to satisfy a claim from assets of the
3 protected series.
4 (12) Record. – Information inscribed on a tangible medium or stored in an
5 electronic or other medium and retrievable in perceivable form.
6 (13) Special deposit. – A deposit that satisfies G.S. 54D-5.
7 (14) State. – A state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico,
8 the United States Virgin Islands, or any other territory or possession subject
9 to the jurisdiction of the United States. The term includes an agency or
10 instrumentality of these entities.
11 "§ 54D-3. Scope; choice of law; forum.
12 (a) This Chapter applies to a special deposit under an account agreement that states the
13 intention of the parties to establish a special deposit governed by this Chapter, regardless of
14 whether a party to the account agreement or a transaction related to the special deposit, or the
15 special deposit itself, has a reasonable relation to this State.
16 (b) The parties to an account agreement may choose a forum in this State for settling a
17 dispute arising out of the special deposit, regardless of whether a party to the account agreement
18 or a transaction related to the special deposit, or the special deposit itself, has a reasonable relation
19 to this State.
20 (c) This Chapter does not affect either of the following:
21 (1) A right or obligation relating to a deposit other than a special deposit under
22 this Chapter.
23 (2) The voidability of a deposit or transfer that is fraudulent or voidable under
24 other law.
25 "§ 54D-4. Variation by agreement or amendment.
26 (a) The effect of G.S. 54D-2 through G.S. 54D-6, G.S. 54D-8 through G.S. 54D-11, and
27 G.S. 54D-14 shall not be varied by agreement, except as provided in those sections. Subject to
28 subsection (b) of this section, the effect of G.S. 54D-7, 54D-12, and 54D-13 may be varied by
29 agreement.
30 (b) A provision in an account agreement or other record that substantially excuses
31 liability or substantially limits remedies for failure to perform an obligation under this Chapter is
32 not sufficient to vary the effect of a provision of this Chapter.
33 (c) If a beneficiary is a party to an account agreement, the bank and the depositor may
34 amend the agreement without the consent of the beneficiary only if the agreement expressly
35 permits the amendment.
36 (d) If a beneficiary is not a party to an account agreement and the bank and the depositor
37 know the beneficiary has knowledge of the agreement's terms, the bank and the depositor may
38 amend the agreement without the consent of the beneficiary only if the amendment does not
39 adversely and materially affect a payment right of the beneficiary.
40 (e) If a beneficiary is not a party to an account agreement and the bank and the depositor
41 do not know whether the beneficiary has knowledge of the agreement's terms, the bank and the
42 depositor may amend the agreement without the consent of the beneficiary only if the amendment
43 is made in good faith.
44 "§ 54D-5. Requirements for special deposit.
45 A deposit is a special deposit if all of the following apply:
46 (1) The deposit is a deposit of funds in a bank under an account agreement.
47 (2) The deposit is for the benefit of at least two beneficiaries, one or more of
48 which may be a depositor.
49 (3) The deposit is denominated in a medium of exchange that is currently
50 authorized or adopted by a domestic or foreign government.
51 (4) The deposit is for a permissible purpose stated in the account agreement.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 203

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (5) The deposit is subject to a contingency.
2 "§ 54D-6. Permissible purpose.
3 (a) A special deposit must serve at least one permissible purpose stated in the account
4 agreement from the time the special deposit is created in the account agreement until termination
5 of the special deposit.
6 (b) If, before termination of the special deposit, the bank or a court determines the special
7 deposit no longer satisfies subsection (a) of this section, G.S. 54D-8 through G.S. 54D-11 cease
8 to apply to any funds deposited in the special deposit after the special deposit ceases to satisfy
9 subsection (a) of this section.
10 (c) If, before termination of a special deposit, the bank determines the special deposit no
11 longer satisfies subsection (a) of this section, the bank may take action it believes is necessary
12 under the circumstances, including terminating the special deposit.
13 "§ 54D-7. Payment to beneficiary by bank.
14 (a) Unless the account agreement provides otherwise, the bank shall discharge its
15 obligation to a beneficiary when it is obligated to pay the beneficiary and there are sufficient
16 actually and finally collected funds in the balance of the special deposit.
17 (b) Except as provided in subsection (c) of this section, the obligation to pay the
18 beneficiary is excused if the funds available in the special deposit are insufficient to cover the
19 payment.
20 (c) Unless the account agreement provides otherwise, if the funds available in the special
21 deposit are insufficient to cover an obligation to pay a beneficiary, a beneficiary may elect to be
22 paid the funds that are available or, if there is more than one beneficiary, a pro rata share of the
23 funds available. Payment to the beneficiary making the election under this subsection discharges
24 the bank's obligation to pay a beneficiary and does not constitute an accord and satisfaction with
25 respect to another person obligated to the beneficiary.
26 (d) Unless the account agreement provides otherwise, the obligation of the bank obligated
27 to pay a beneficiary is immediately due and payable.
28 (e) The bank may discharge its obligation under this section by doing either of the
29 following:
30 (1) Crediting another transaction account of the beneficiary.
31 (2) Taking other action that either is permitted under the account agreement for
32 the bank to obtain a discharge or otherwise would constitute a discharge under
33 law.
34 (f) If the bank obligated to pay a beneficiary has incurred an obligation to discharge the
35 obligation of another person, the obligation of the other person is discharged if action by the bank
36 under subsection (e) of this section would constitute a discharge of the obligation of the other
37 person under law that determines whether an obligation is satisfied.
38 "§ 54D-8. Property interest of depositor or beneficiary.
39 (a) Neither a depositor nor a beneficiary has a property interest in a special deposit.
40 (b) Any property interest with respect to a special deposit is only in the right to receive
41 payment if the bank is obligated to pay a beneficiary and not in the special deposit itself. Any
42 property interest under this subsection is determined under other law.
43 "§ 54D-9. When creditor process enforceable against bank.
44 (a) Subject to subsection (b) of this section, creditor process with respect to a special
45 deposit is not enforceable against the bank holding the special deposit.
46 (b) Creditor process is enforceable against the bank holding a special deposit with respect
47 to an amount the bank is obligated to pay a beneficiary or a depositor if all of the following apply:
48 (1) The process is served on the bank.
49 (2) The process provides sufficient information to permit the bank to identify the
50 depositor or the beneficiary from the bank's books and records.
51 (3) The process gives the bank a reasonable opportunity to act on the process.
Page 204 House Bill 40-Fourth Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (c) Creditor process served on a bank before it is enforceable against the bank under
2 subsection (b) of this section does not create a right of the creditor against the bank or a duty of
3 the bank to the creditor. Other law determines whether creditor process creates a lien enforceable
4 against the beneficiary on a contingent interest of a beneficiary, including a depositor as a
5 beneficiary, even if not enforceable against the bank.
6 "§ 54D-10. Injunction or similar relief.
7 A court may enjoin, or grant similar relief that would have the effect of enjoining, a bank
8 from paying a depositor or beneficiary only if payment would constitute a material fraud or
9 facilitate a material fraud with respect to a special deposit.
10 "§ 54D-11. Recoupment or set off.
11 (a) Except as provided in subsection (b) or (c) of this section, a bank shall not exercise a
12 right of recoupment or set off against a special deposit.
13 (b) An account agreement may authorize the bank to debit the special deposit in any of
14 the following circumstances:
15 (1) When the bank becomes obligated to pay a beneficiary, in an amount that does
16 not exceed the amount necessary to discharge the obligation.
17 (2) For a fee assessed by the bank that relates to an overdraft in the special deposit
18 account.
19 (3) For costs incurred by the bank that relate directly to the special deposit.
20 (4) To reverse an earlier credit posted by the bank to the balance of the special
21 deposit account, if the reversal occurs under an event or circumstance
22 warranted under other law of this State governing mistake and restitution.
23 (c) The bank holding a special deposit may exercise a right of recoupment or set off
24 against an obligation to pay a beneficiary, even if the bank funds payment from the special
25 deposit.
26 "§ 54D-12. Duties and liability of bank.
27 (a) A bank does not have a fiduciary duty to any person with respect to a special deposit.
28 (b) When the bank holding a special deposit becomes obligated to pay a beneficiary, a
29 debtor-creditor relationship arises between the bank and beneficiary.
30 (c) The bank holding a special deposit has a duty to a beneficiary to comply with the
31 account agreement and this Chapter.
32 (d) If the bank holding a special deposit does not comply with the account agreement or
33 this Chapter, the bank is liable to a depositor or beneficiary only for damages proximately caused
34 by the noncompliance. Except as provided by other law of this State, the bank is not liable for
35 consequential, special, or punitive damages.
36 (e) The bank holding a special deposit may rely on records presented in compliance with
37 the account agreement to determine whether the bank is obligated to pay a beneficiary.
38 (f) If the account agreement requires payment on presentation of a record, the bank shall
39 determine within a reasonable time whether the record is sufficient to require payment. If the
40 agreement requires action by the bank on presentation of a record, the bank is not liable for
41 relying in good faith on the genuineness of the record if the record appears on its face to be
42 genuine.
43 (g) Unless the account agreement provides otherwise, the bank is not required to
44 determine whether a permissible purpose stated in the agreement continues to exist.
45 "§ 54D-13. Term and termination.
46 (a) Unless otherwise provided in the account agreement, a special deposit terminates five
47 years after the date the special deposit was first funded.
48 (b) Unless otherwise provided in the account agreement, if the bank cannot identify or
49 locate a beneficiary entitled to payment when the special deposit is terminated, and a balance
50 remains in the special deposit, the bank shall pay the balance to the depositor or depositors as a
51 beneficiary or beneficiaries.
House Bill 40-Fourth Edition Page 205

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (c) A bank that pays the remaining balance as provided under subsection (b) of this
2 section has no further obligation with respect to the special deposit.
3 "§ 54D-14. Principles of law and equity.
4 Chapter 25 ("Uniform Commercial Code") of the General Statutes, G.S. 1A-1, Rule 22
5 ("Interpleader"), consumer protection law, law governing deposits generally, law related to
6 escheat and abandoned or unclaimed property, and the principles of law and equity, including
7 law related to capacity to contract, principal and agent, estoppel, fraud, misrepresentation, duress,
8 coercion, mistake, and bankruptcy, supplement this Chapter except to the extent inconsistent with
9 this Chapter.
10 "§ 54D-15. Uniformity of application and construction.
11 In applying and construing this Chapter, a court shall consider the promotion of uniformity
12 of the law among jurisdictions that enact the Uniform Special Deposits Act."
13 SECTION 159. The Revisor of Statutes shall cause to be printed, as annotations to
14 the published General Statutes, all relevant portions of the Official Comments to the Uniform
15 Special Deposits Act and all explanatory comments of the drafters of this Part as the Revisor may
16 deem appropriate.
17 SECTION 160. This Part becomes effective October 1, 2025, and applies to a special
18 deposit made under an account agreement executed on or after that date.
